2x" data-file-width="462" data-file-height="438" /></a></div>\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of Prime Ministers of the United Kingdom</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:148px;max-width:148px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:183px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert-Walpole-1st-Earl-of-Orford.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Robert-Walpole-1st-Earl-of-Orford.jpg/219px-Robert-Walpole-1st-Earl-of-Orford.jpg 1.5x, /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:140px;max-width:140px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:183px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:OlderPittThe_Younger_crop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/OlderPittThe_Younger_crop.jpg/138px-OlderPittThe_Younger_crop.jpg" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/OlderPittThe_Younger_crop.jpg/276px-OlderPittThe_Younger_crop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1157" data-file-height="1541" /></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:138px;max-width:138px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:193px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Benjamin_Disraeli_by_W%26D_Downey,_c1878.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Benjamin_Disraeli_by_W%26D_Downey%2C_c1878.jpg/136px-Benjamin_Disraeli_by_W%26D_Downey%2C_c1878.jpg" width="136" height="194" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Benjamin_Disraeli_by_W%26D_Downey%2C_c1878.jpg/204px-Benjamin_Disraeli_by_W%26D_Downey%2C_c1878.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Benjamin_Disraeli_by_W%26D_Downey%2C_c1878.jpg/272px-Benjamin_Disraeli_by_W%26D_Downey%2C_c1878.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1121" data-file-height="1600" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:150px;max-width:150px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:193px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Sir_Henry_Campbell-Bannerman.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Sir_Henry_Campbell-Bannerman.jpg/148px-Sir_Henry_Campbell-Bannerman.jpg" width="148" height="193" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Sir_Henry_Campbell-Bannerman.jpg/222px-Sir_Henry_Campbell-Bannerman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Sir_Henry_Campbell-Bannerman.jpg/296px-Sir_Henry_Campbell-Bannerman.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1904" data-file-height="2484" /></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><div><ul><li>Top left: <a href="/wiki/Robert_Walpole" title="Robert Walpole">Robert Walpole</a> was the first Prime Minister of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a>.</li><li>Top right: <a href="/wiki/William_Pitt_the_Younger" title="William Pitt the Younger">William Pitt the Younger</a> was the first Prime Minister of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom</a>.</li><li>Bottom left: <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Disraeli" title="Benjamin Disraeli">Benjamin Disraeli</a> was the first Prime Minister to officially use the title.</li><li>Bottom right: <a href="/wiki/Henry_Campbell-Bannerman" title="Henry Campbell-Bannerman">Henry Campbell-Bannerman</a> was the first Prime Minister to officially hold the title.</li></ul></div></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister of the United Kingdom</a> is the head of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom">Government of the United Kingdom</a>, and chairs <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Cabinet of the United Kingdom">Cabinet</a> meetings. There is no specific date for when the office of Prime Minister first appeared, as the role was not created but rather evolved over a period of time through a merger of duties.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHennessy200139\xe2\x80\x9340_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHennessy200139\xe2\x80\x9340-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The term had been used in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_Great_Britain" title="House of Commons of Great Britain">House of Commons</a> as early as 1805,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECastlereagh1805_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECastlereagh1805-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and it was certainly in parliamentary use by the 1880s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEardley-Wilmot1885Macfarlane1885_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEardley-Wilmot1885Macfarlane1885-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> In 1905 the post of Prime Minister was officially given recognition in the <a href="/wiki/Orders_of_precedence_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Orders of precedence in the United Kingdom">order of precedence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarriott192383_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarriott192383-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Modern historians generally consider <a href="/wiki/Sir_Robert_Walpole" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Robert Walpole">Sir Robert Walpole</a>, who led the government of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a> for over twenty years from 1721,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClarke1999266Hennessy200139\xe2\x80\x9340_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClarke1999266Hennessy200139\xe2\x80\x9340-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> as the first Prime Minister. Walpole is also the longest-serving British prime minister by this definition.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News1998_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News1998-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Sir_Henry_Campbell-Bannerman" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Henry Campbell-Bannerman">Sir Henry Campbell-Bannerman</a> was the first and <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a> the longest-serving Prime Minister officially referred to as such in the order of precedence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMackay1987Marriott192383_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMackay1987Marriott192383-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The first to officially use the title was <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Disraeli" title="Benjamin Disraeli">Benjamin Disraeli</a>, who signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Berlin_(1878)" title="Treaty of Berlin (1878)">Treaty of Berlin</a> as "Prime Minister of her Britannic Majesty" in 1878.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBogdanor1997_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBogdanor1997-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Strictly, the first Prime Minister of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom (of Great Britain and Ireland)</a> was <a href="/wiki/William_Pitt_the_Younger" title="William Pitt the Younger">William Pitt the Younger</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurt1874106Castlereagh1805_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurt1874106Castlereagh1805-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The first Prime Minister of the current United Kingdom, i.e. the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland, was <a href="/wiki/Bonar_Law" title="Bonar Law">Bonar Law</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaw1922_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaw1922-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> although the country was not renamed officially until 1927, when <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Baldwin" title="Stanley Baldwin">Stanley Baldwin</a> was the serving Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoyal_and_Parliamentary_Titles_Act1927_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoyal_and_Parliamentary_Titles_Act1927-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Due to the gradual evolution of the post of Prime Minister, the title is applied to early prime ministers only retrospectively;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeonard20101_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeonard20101-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> this has sometimes given rise to academic dispute. <a href="/wiki/William_Pulteney,_1st_Earl_of_Bath" title="William Pulteney, 1st Earl of Bath">Lord Bath</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Waldegrave,_2nd_Earl_Waldegrave" title="James Waldegrave, 2nd Earl Waldegrave">Lord Waldegrave</a> are sometimes listed as prime ministers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarpenter199237_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarpenter199237-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Bath was invited to <a href="/wiki/Short-lived_ministry" title="Short-lived ministry">form a ministry</a> by <a href="/wiki/George_II_of_Great_Britain" title="George II of Great Britain"><span class="nowrap">George II</span></a> when <a href="/wiki/Henry_Pelham" title="Henry Pelham">Henry Pelham</a> resigned in 1746,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeonard201047_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeonard201047-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> as was Waldegrave in 1757 after the dismissal of <a href="/wiki/William_Pitt_the_Elder" class="mw-redirect" title="William Pitt the Elder">William Pitt the Elder</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeonard201065_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeonard201065-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> who dominated the affairs of government <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_in_the_Seven_Years%27_War" title="Great Britain in the Seven Years&#39; War">during the Seven Years\' War</a>. Neither was able to command sufficient parliamentary support to form a government; Bath stepped down after two days,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarpenter199237_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarpenter199237-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> and Waldegrave after three.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeonard201065_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeonard201065-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Modern academic consensus does not consider either man to have held office as Prime Minister,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Oxford_Dictionary_of_National_Biography&#39;&#39;2011_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Oxford_Dictionary_of_National_Biography&#39;&#39;2011-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and they are therefore not listed.\n</p>\n<div class="toclimit-3"><div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Before_1721">Before 1721</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Before 1721">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_chief_ministers" title="List of English chief ministers">List of English chief ministers</a></div>\n<p>Prior to the <a href="/wiki/Georgian_era" title="Georgian era">Georgian era</a>, the <a href="/wiki/HM_Treasury" title="HM Treasury">Treasury</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England</a> was led by the <a href="/wiki/Lord_High_Treasurer" title="Lord High Treasurer">Lord High Treasurer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911f_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911f-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> By the late <a href="/wiki/Tudor_period" title="Tudor period">Tudor period</a>, the Lord High Treasurer was regarded as one of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Officers_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Officers of State">Great Officers of State</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911f_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911f-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and was often (though not always) the dominant figure in government: <a href="/wiki/Edward_Seymour,_1st_Duke_of_Somerset" title="Edward Seymour, 1st Duke of Somerset">Edward Seymour, 1st Duke of Somerset</a> (Lord High Treasurer, 1547\xe2\x80\x931549),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPollard1904_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPollard1904-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> served as <a href="/wiki/Lord_Protector" title="Lord Protector">Lord Protector</a> to his prepubescent nephew <a href="/wiki/Edward_VI_of_England" title="Edward VI of England"><span class="nowrap">Edward VI</span></a>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPollard1904_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPollard1904-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/William_Cecil,_1st_Baron_Burghley" title="William Cecil, 1st Baron Burghley">William Cecil, 1st Baron Burghley</a> (Lord High Treasurer, 1572\xe2\x80\x931598),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911a_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911a-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> was the dominant <a href="/wiki/List_of_ministers_to_Queen_Elizabeth_I" title="List of ministers to Queen Elizabeth I">minister to <span class="nowrap">Elizabeth I</span></a>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911a_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911a-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Burghley\'s son <a href="/wiki/Robert_Cecil,_1st_Earl_of_Salisbury" title="Robert Cecil, 1st Earl of Salisbury">Robert Cecil, 1st Earl of Salisbury</a>, succeeded his father as chief minister to <span class="nowrap">Elizabeth I</span> (1598\xe2\x80\x931603) and was eventually appointed by <a href="/wiki/James_VI_and_I" title="James VI and I"><span class="nowrap">James I</span></a> as Lord High Treasurer (1608\xe2\x80\x931612).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911c_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911c-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the late <a href="/wiki/Stuart_period" title="Stuart period">Stuart period</a>, the Treasury was often run not by a single individual, i.e. Lord High Treasurer, but by a <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/commission#Noun" class="extiw" title="wikt:commission">commission</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lords_of_the_Treasury" class="mw-redirect" title="Lords of the Treasury">Lords of the Treasury</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChapman2002_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChapman2002-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> led by the <a href="/wiki/First_Lord_of_the_Treasury" title="First Lord of the Treasury">First Lord of the Treasury</a>. The last Lords High Treasurer, <a href="/wiki/Lord_Godolphin" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Godolphin">Lord Godolphin</a> (1702\xe2\x80\x931710) and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Harley,_1st_Earl_of_Oxford_and_Earl_Mortimer" title="Robert Harley, 1st Earl of Oxford and Earl Mortimer">Lord Oxford</a> (1711\xe2\x80\x931714),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFisher_Russell_Barker1890Stephen1890_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFisher_Russell_Barker1890Stephen1890-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> ran the government of <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Queen_of_Great_Britain" title="Anne, Queen of Great Britain">Queen Anne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorrill2018_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorrill2018-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the succession of <a href="/wiki/George_I_of_Great_Britain" title="George I of Great Britain"><span class="nowrap">George I</span></a> in 1714, the arrangement of a commission of Lords of the Treasury (as opposed to a single Lord High Treasurer) became permanent.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChapman200215_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChapman200215-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> For the next three years, the government was headed by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Townshend,_2nd_Viscount_Townshend" title="Charles Townshend, 2nd Viscount Townshend">Lord Townshend</a>, who was appointed <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_the_Northern_Department" title="Secretary of State for the Northern Department">Secretary of State for the Northern Department</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcMullen_Rigg1899_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcMullen_Rigg1899-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Subsequently, <a href="/wiki/James_Stanhope,_1st_Earl_Stanhope" title="James Stanhope, 1st Earl Stanhope">Lord Stanhope</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Spencer,_3rd_Earl_of_Sunderland" title="Charles Spencer, 3rd Earl of Sunderland">Lord Sunderland</a> ran the government jointly,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911dChisholm1911e_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911dChisholm1911e-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> with Stanhope managing foreign affairs and Sunderland domestic.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911dChisholm1911e_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911dChisholm1911e-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Stanhope died in February 1721 and Sunderland resigned two months later;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911dChisholm1911e_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911dChisholm1911e-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Townshend and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Walpole" title="Robert Walpole">Robert Walpole</a> were then invited to form the next government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911bMcMullen_Rigg1899_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911bMcMullen_Rigg1899-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> From that point, the holder of the <em>office</em> of First Lord also usually (albeit unofficially) held the status of Prime Minister. It was not until the <a href="/wiki/Edwardian_era" title="Edwardian era">Edwardian era</a> that the title <em><a href="/wiki/Prime_minister" title="Prime minister">prime minister</a></em> was constitutionally recognised.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeonard20101_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeonard20101-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The Prime Minister still holds the office of First Lord by constitutional convention,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUK_Government2013_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUK_Government2013-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> the only exceptions being <a href="/wiki/Lord_Chatham" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Chatham">Lord Chatham</a> (1766\xe2\x80\x931768) and <a href="/wiki/Lord_Salisbury" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Salisbury">Lord Salisbury</a> (1885\xe2\x80\x931886, 1887\xe2\x80\x931892, 1895\xe2\x80\x931902).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnglefieldSeatonWhite1995413Locker-Lampson1907497_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnglefieldSeatonWhite1995413Locker-Lampson1907497-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Since_1721">Since 1721</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Since 1721">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="toc" style="line-height:normal; padding-bottom:0.5em; margin-left:5em">\n<caption class="hlist" style="padding-left:1.6em">\n<ul><li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Peer"><b><a href="#ref_Peer">^\xc2\xa7</a></b>&#160;Elevated to the <a id="cite_note-Mandate-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Mandate_30-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Legend for the cells listed in the sixth column from right:<div class="plainlist" style="padding-left:1.6em"><ul><li>e.g. <span style="background-color:#ffe5b4; color: #002bb8; border:1px solid #AAAAAA; text-align:center;">&#160;1722&#160;</span> and <span style="background-color:#def; color: #002bb8; border:1px solid #AAAAAA; text-align:center;">&#160;1841&#160;</span>\xe2\x80\x94coloured containing a linked year, indicates general elections won by the government (see 1722) or those that led to its formation (see 1841);</li><li>e.g. <span style="background-color:#ddd; color: #002bb8; border:1px solid #AAAAAA; text-align:center;">&#160;1830&#160;</span>\xe2\x80\x94shaded grey containing a linked year, indicates elections held resulting in no single party winning a majority in the Commons;</li><li>e.g. <span style="background-color:#d2d2f3; color:black; border:1px solid #AAAAAA; text-align:center;">&#160;\xe2\x80\x94&#160;</span>\xe2\x80\x94coloured containing a dash, indicates the formation of a <a href="/wiki/Majority_government" title="Majority government">majority government</a> without an election;</li><li>e.g. <span style="background-color:#ddd; color:black; border:1px solid #AAAAAA; text-align:center;">&#160;\xe2\x80\x94&#160;</span>\xe2\x80\x94shaded grey containing a dash, indicates the formation of a <a href="/wiki/Minority_government" title="Minority government">minority government</a> or a <a href="/wiki/Coalition_government" title="Coalition government">coalition government</a> during a <a href="/wiki/Hung_parliament" title="Hung parliament">hung parliament</a>.</li></ul></div></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Regent-37"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Regent_37-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">George III appointed all but one of his fourteen prime ministers. His son <a href="/wiki/George_IV_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George IV of the United Kingdom">George, Prince of Wales</a>, served as Prince Regent <a href="/wiki/Regency_era" title="Regency era">from 8 February 1811</a> (<a href="#CITEREFPrydeGreenwayPorterRoy1996">Pryde et al. 1996</a>, p.&#160;47); it was the Regent who appointed Liverpool as Prime Minister in 1812 (<a href="#CITEREFEnglefieldSeatonWhite1995">Englefield, Seaton &amp; White 1995</a>, p.&#160;363), rather than the monarch.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Douglas-Home-92"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Douglas-Home_92-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Douglas Home disclaimed his peerage as the <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Home" title="Earl of Home">Earl of Home</a> on 23 October 1963. He was <a href="/wiki/Kinross_and_Western_Perthshire_by-election,_1963" title="Kinross and Western Perthshire by-election, 1963">elected an MP</a> on 7 November.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
